open satellite imagery such as Landsat (NASA/USGS) and Sentinel (ESA) to monitor land and its nature-based carbon at a global scale. The new datasets will enable stakeholders to take on the challenges from the global land-squeeze, combat climate change, protect biodiversity, and improve people\xe2\x80\x99s lives. This is achieved by monitoring the world\xe2\x80\x99s land and its nature-based carbon, so data can turn into, and generate insights for collective accountability.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eAs a Founding Partner, Resource Watch contributes by presenting, processing, and visualizing key datasets of the Land \\u0026amp; Carbon Lab initiative on the Resource Watch platform. This data enables users to view forest-related carbon dynamics at any scale, providing a detailed understanding of how various forested areas are contributing to global emissions and Seasonal Global Land Cover\\u003c/h5\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eLand \\u0026amp; Carbon Lab, is partnering with Google and the National Geographic Society, on a project to leverage advanced artificial intelligence methods and large training datasets to develop a global land cover dataset at an unprecedented 10-meter resolution. The dataset, which is still in preparation, will cover nine land cover classes and is based on Sentinel-2 satellite imagery. With a dataset of such high-resolution, community organizations, governments and researchers will be able to better understand seasonal and intra-annual seasonal land cover changes.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eThe dataset will become available on Resource Watch.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-028ddaf class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eResource Watch is partnering with the Global Commons Alliance, to launch \\u003ca href=\\"http://earthhq.org\\"\\u003eEarth HQ\\u003c/a\\u003e, a new interactive site to visualize and understand the climate and nature crisis. Presented in Glasgow at COP 26, Earth HQ offers a creative blend of near-real time data, environmental science journalism, and compelling multimedia storytelling\xe2\x80\x93all on a user-friendly digital timely site.\\u0026nbsp;\\u003cspan style=\\"font-family: var( --e-global-typography-text-font-family ), Sans-serif; font-weight: var( --e-global-typography-text-font-weight ); font-size: 1rem;\\"\\u003eResource Watch contributes data visualizations of timely trusted data, data integrity, and design advice.\\u0026nbsp;\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-36f4b11 elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"36f4b11\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eEarth HQ is a new interactive site that enables the concerned public, journalists and NGOs to better understand the climate planetary emergency, by linking relevant climate-related data to the live events happening in the world. Its user-friendly interface allows users to interact with the latest data and insights on the state of our global commons across climate, freshwater, forest, ocean, and biodiversity. Earth HQ presents a \xe2\x80\x98situation room for the planet\xe2\x80\x99 that combines the rigor of near real-time scientific data and engaging visualization with the storytelling power of environmental journalism.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eResource Watch provides its catalogue of key datasets and visualizations for Earth HQ to track the status of earth systems and pressures, providing global regularly updated, trusted data that is needed for monitoring critical threats to the global commons and track progress towards solutions.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-4f1262b0 Alliance\\u003c/strong\\u003e \\u003cbr /\\u003eEarth HQ was created as part of the Global Commons Alliance (GCA), as a platform to utilize media and data to inform and mobilize the public. The four GCA components are: the Earth Commission, a a high-level scientific advisory body; the Science Based Targets Network, which supports companies, cities and governments in setting targets informed by planetary boundaries; the Systems Change Lab, which will identify and monitor the systemic revolutions needed to make such targets achievable; and the Earth HQ.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-69569dbb elementor-widget data-element_type=\\"column\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-column-wrap elementor-element-populated\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-wrap\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-6b0f6ba elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"6b0f6ba\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003eMore than 80% of the world\xe2\x80\x99s cities do not meet World Health Organization standards for safe air, making air pollution the world\xe2\x80\x99s top environmental risk for health.  The growing air pollution problem is having enormous impacts on human well-being including the propensity to contract respiratory infections, heart disease, stroke and lung cancer. Air pollution caused by human activities like the burning of fossil fuels is also linked to the near-term warming of the atmosphere. Thus, reducing air pollution can have almost immediate health and climate benefits.\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-bb4432a elementor-widget elementor-widget-html\\" data-id=\\"bb4432a\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"html.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv\\u003e\\n    \\u003ciframe src=\\"https://resourcewatch.org/embed/map/afcb9734-77d5-447f-9278-c29bbf07b07c\\" width=\\"100%\\" height=\\"500px\\" frameBorder=\\"0\\" \\u003e\\u003c/iframe\\u003e\\n\\u003c/div\\u003e\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-a4d7ea9 elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"a4d7ea9\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cem\\u003eFigure 1. The map shows the population per country exposed to harmful levels of PM2.5 particles, from 1990 to 2017. Source: Resource Watch, based on data from the World Bank and the World Health Organization.\\n\\u003c/em\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-2eb9a32 elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"2eb9a32\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eDespite the multiple reasons to reduce air pollution around the world, many cities, particularly in low- and middle-income countries, lack the data management tools as well as financial and human resources to improve their air quality. If cities could gain access to high-resolution visualized forecasts, city governments would be able to design better interventions and control policies, civil society could monitor compliance with city policies and residents can act based on real-time information.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-f9ac998 elementor-widget elementor-widget-heading\\" data-id=\\"f9ac998\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"heading.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\u003ch2 class=\\"elementor-heading-title elementor-size-default\\"\\u003e\\u003cb\\u003eCity AQ: A localized solution   \\u003c/b\\u003e\\u003c/h2\\u003e\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-6624d36 elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"6624d36\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eThe \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.wri.org/initiatives/cityaq\\"\\u003eCityAQ\\u003c/a\\u003e project was conceived to provide reliable, locally relevant, accessible air quality forecasts data and visualizations to resource-constrained cities facing air quality challenges, by leveraging the data available from local monitoring networks and global forecasts. CityAQ utilizes the tools and expertise of the National Aeronautics and Space Administration\xe2\x80\x99s (NASA) in collaboration with local experts in participating cities, WRI and other organizations such as \\u003ca href=\\"https://openaq.org/#/\\"\\u003eOpenAQ\\u003c/a\\u003e.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eWRI, NASA, and cities collaborated to develop CityAQ, combining global models with data from local air quality monitoring networks to produce optimized forecasts with spatial and temporal resolutions useful for local decision making.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eIn a pilot phase, WRI identified a set of cities in Latin America, Africa and Asia that could benefit from these air quality forecasts. The selection required cities to have continuous and systematic monitoring using regulatory-grade instruments for ozone (O3), nitrogen dioxide (NO2) and particulate matter less than 2.5 micrometers (PM2.5), as well as hourly observations valid from 2018 onwards. The final set included the following cities:\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cul\\u003e\\u003cli\\u003eJakarta, Indonesia\\u003c/li\\u003e\\u003cli\\u003eAddis Ababa, Ethiopia\\u003c/li\\u003e\\u003cli\\u003eGuadalajara (Metropolitan Area), Mexico\\u003c/li\\u003e\\u003cli\\u003eMonterrey (Metropolitan Area), Mexico\\u003c/li\\u003e\\u003cli\\u003eGuanajuato State, Mexico\\u003c/li\\u003e\\u003cli\\u003eBogota, Colombia\\u003c/li\\u003e\\u003cli\\u003eSao Paolo, Brazil\\u003c/li\\u003e\\u003c/ul\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003e\xc2\xa0\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eWRI\\u0026#8217;s Air Quality team has worked with air quality experts in these cities, preparing and sharing data from their local monitoring stations, which would then be used to generate the adjusted CityAQ forecasts. In the process, WRI helped facilitate greater access to available global air quality information by including the local air quality\xc2\xa0data in the air quality platform OpenAQ and WRI\xe2\x80\x99s Resource Watch platform.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-aabd7b7 elementor-widget elementor-widget-heading\\" data-id=\\"aabd7b7\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"heading.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\u003ch2 class=\\"elementor-heading-title elementor-size-default\\"\\u003eTracking Air Pollutants\\u003c/h2\\u003e\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-2cbbfb4 elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"2cbbfb4\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eTransport and other urban activities emit large amounts of pollutants into the atmosphere which, depending on meteorological conditions, can remain over the city for some time or be quickly transported to other regions. In the atmosphere, pollutants are gradually transformed into species of greater toxicity than those that gave rise to them. The 3 main pollutants that are the subject of CityAQ\xe2\x80\x99s forecasts are:\\u003c/p\\u003e\\n\\u003cul\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003eNitrogen dioxide (NO\xe2\x82\x82)(\xc2\xb9): one of a group of highly reactive gases known as nitrogen oxides (NOx). NO is used as the indicator for the larger group of nitrogen oxides. NO\xe2\x82\x82 primarily gets in the air from the burning of fuel.\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003eTropospheric ozone (O\xe2\x82\x83)(\xc2\xb2): Ozone at ground level is a harmful air pollutant because of its effects on people and the environment, and it is the main ingredient in \xe2\x80\x9csmog\\u0026#8221;. It is a secondary gas formed by the interaction of sunlight with hydrocarbons and nitrogen oxides, which are emitted by vehicles, fossil fuel power plants, and other manmade sources.\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003cli\\u003eParticulate matter (PM\xe2\x82\x82.\xe2\x82\x85)(\xc2\xb3): refers to solid and liquid particles that are suspended in the air. These are predominantly the result of fossil fuel combustion. PM2.5 refers to particles with diameter less than 2.5 \xce\xbcm\xe2\x80\x943% the diameter of a human hair.\\u003c/li\\u003e\\n\\u003c/ul\\u003e\\n\\u003cp\\u003eAs of June 2021, the daily updated forecasts generated by CityAQ for \\u003ca href=\\"https://resourcewatch.org/data/explore/cit004crw0nrt-Air-Quality-Ozone-O-Station-Forecasts\\"\\u003eO3\\u003c/a\\u003e, \\u003ca href=\\"https://resourcewatch.org/data/explore/cit004brw0nrt-Air-Quality-Nitrogen-Dioxide-NO-Station-Forecasts\\"\\u003eNO2\\u003c/a\\u003e and \\u003ca href=\\"https://resourcewatch.org/data/explore/cit004rw0-City-AQ-Forecasts\\"\\u003ePM2.5\\u003c/a\\u003e are publicly available and visualized on Resource Watch\xe2\x80\x99s open data platform. This platform also offers tools that allow users to access other social and environmental datasets from the vast catalog to generate valuable insight into air quality issues in a quick and intuitive way. Forecast visualizations on Resource Watch can be easily embedded into other websites, such as official web pages of participating cities.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-a842e6b elementor-widget elementor-widget-heading\\" data-id=\\"a842e6b\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"heading.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\u003ch2 class=\\"elementor-heading-title elementor-size-default\\"\\u003eHow CityAQ Works \\u003c/h2\\u003e\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-dbfd61b elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"dbfd61b\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003eAir quality management can be very disparate from one city to another, depending on their budgets and capacities. To properly manage air quality, environmental authorities traditionally rely on a key tool for generating information: monitoring networks instrumented with regulatory-grade equipment.\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003csection class=\\"elementor-section elementor-inner-section elementor-element elementor-element-503cb8a elementor-section-boxed elementor-section-height-default elementor-section-height-default\\" data-id=\\"503cb8a\\" data-element_type=\\"section\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-container elementor-column-gap-default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-row\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-column elementor-col-50 elementor-inner-column elementor-element elementor-element-aca86d6\\" data-id=\\"aca86d6\\" data-element_type=\\"column\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-column-wrap elementor-element-populated\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-wrap\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-989bf85 elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"989bf85\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eSome cities also employ models for air quality forecasting and diagnostic purposes. Air quality forecasts are very valuable as they allow governments and the public to take informed action. With adequate communication of the data and visualizations from these forecasts, people are able to protect themselves from risk, especially those who are more susceptible to variation in air quality, such as those with respiratory or cardiovascular conditions, young children, and pregnant women. Mexico City is a good example of this: The local government has developed \\u003ca href=\\"http://www.aire.cdmx.gob.mx/pronostico-aire/sobre-modelo.php\\"\\u003etheir own forecast\\u003c/a\\u003e, combining a weather model, an emissions model, and a chemical transport model.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eForecasts allow decision-makers to proactively plan to mitigate the effects of a pollution event in different ways: warning the population, alerting their health systems, canceling outdoor events or reducing emissions that would exacerbate conditions. They also allow them to estimate the behavior of pollutants during an event originating outside their jurisdiction. The forecast is a key element that allows authorities to design and enforce control strategies to achieve systemic reductions in air pollution.\\u003cbr /\\u003eWhile not all cities currently have forecast models developed specifically for their city, global air quality tools, such as the \\u003ca href=\\"https://gmao.gsfc.nasa.gov/weather_prediction/GEOS-CF/\\"\\u003eGoddard Earth Observing System Composition Forecast (GEOS-CF)\\u003c/a\\u003e allow for the unprecedented opportunity to access continuously updated air quality forecasts anywhere in the world. However, these global models have a coarse spatial resolution for city management purposes (e.g., GEOS resolution is 25 x 25 km2), which makes it difficult to identify local phenomena that will affect air quality in the city.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv Source: GMAO-NASA.  \\n\\u003c/em\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-cae90f4 elementor-widget elementor-widget-heading\\" data-id=\\"cae90f4\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"heading.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\u003ch2 class=\\"elementor-heading-title elementor-size-default\\"\\u003eCityAQ In Action\\u003c/h2\\u003e\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-4accf45 elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"4accf45\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eThroughout the pilot phase, the need and importance of producing quality data has been emphasized, not only for regulatory purposes but also for other purposes such as modeling, visualization and evaluation of emerging technologies (e.g., satellite data, low-cost sensors). class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\tby \\u003ca href=\\"https://blog.resourcewatch.org/author/becky-atkinswri-org/\\" title=\\"Posts by Becky Atkins\\" class=\\"author url fn\\" rel=\\"author\\"\\u003eKatie Wood\\u003c/a\\u003e and \\u003ca href=\\"https://blog.resourcewatch.org/author/jonathan-baineswri-org/\\" title=\\"Posts by Jon Baines\\" class=\\"author url fn\\" rel=\\"author\\"\\u003eJon Baines\\u003c/a\\u003e\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-shortcode\\"\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\u003c/section\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003csection data-id=\\"3ee0a446\\" data-element_type=\\"section\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-container elementor-column-gap-default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-row\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-column elementor-col-100 elementor-top-column elementor-element elementor-element-58915172\\" data-id=\\"58915172\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003e\\u003ci\\u003eThis article was originaly posted on WRI\\u0026#8217;s \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.wri.org/insights/inclusive-data-platform-ocean-management\\"\\u003eInsights blog\\u003c/a\\u003e.\\u003c/i\\u003e\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-551886df elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"551886df\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eThe ocean is the world\xe2\x80\x99s largest biome and one of its most valuable resources. It is also the most difficult to monitor, understand and manage, largely due to a lack of data. This is in part due to the sheer vastness of the ocean which covers \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.un.org/sustainabledevelopment/wp-content/uploads/2017/05/Ocean-fact-sheet-package.pdf\\"\\u003e72% of the Earth\xe2\x80\x99s surface\\u003c/a\\u003e and has depths up to 11,034 m (36,201 ft). Moreover, spanning that space are billions of species which interact to form a myriad of ecosystems, many of which are still unknown or poorly understood.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eBut understanding the ocean and its environs is well worth the effort. More than \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.fao.org/3/I9540EN/i9540en.pdf\\"\\u003e3 billion people\\u003c/a\\u003e rely on the ocean as a major source of protein, and ocean-based industries like fishing, offshore energy, shipping and coastal tourism contribute \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.oceanpanel.org/Economicanalysis\\"\\u003eat least 3.5 to 7% of the world\xe2\x80\x99s gross domestic product\\u003c/a\\u003e. This contribution is predicted to double by 2030.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eThe ocean is also increasingly at risk. Processes like \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/B9780128229316000290\\"\\u003edeforestation \\u003c/a\\u003eand \\u003ca href=\\"https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s12237-019-00597-z\\"\\u003eurbanization \\u003c/a\\u003eincrease the flow of pollution, resulting in the degradation of coastal ecosystems. In addition, climate change and unprecedented carbon emissions are changing the \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.science.org/doi/full/10.1126/science.1159124\\"\\u003echemistry \\u003c/a\\u003eand \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.science.org/doi/abs/10.1126/science.aav7619\\"\\u003eaverage temperatures\\u003c/a\\u003e of the ocean, causing further damage to vital ecosystems.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eBetter data is urgently needed by the ocean community to improve management policies that govern decisions such as the selection of marine protected areas, and policies on integrated coastal zone management. For example, people currently working in these areas struggle to integrate data on nutrient and sediment pollution with information on how people are using ocean resources to drive truly sustainable decisions.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eA new tool aims to support people in maintaining and restoring the health of the ocean and the wealth derived from it. In 2020 WRI began efforts to understand how to put data at the heart of ocean sustainability. The resulting \\u003ca href=\\"https://resourcewatch.org/dashboards/ocean-watch\\"\\u003eOcean Watch\\u003c/a\\u003e data platform \\u003cspan class=\\"TextRun SCXW236243878 BCX0\\" lang=\\"EN-GB\\" xml:lang=\\"EN-GB\\" data-contrast=\\"auto\\"\\u003e\\u003cspan class=\\"NormalTextRun SCXW236243878 BCX0\\" data-ccp-charstyle=\\"eop\\" data-ccp-charstyle-defn=\\"{\\u0026quot;ObjectId\\u0026quot;:\\u0026quot;6667d38c-8ac8-4f01-a3ed-b3f96323255f|69\\u0026quot;,\\u0026quot;ClassId\\u0026quot;:1073872969,\\u0026quot;Properties\\u0026quot;:[134233614,\\u0026quot;true\\u0026quot;,201340122,\\u0026quot;1\\u0026quot;,469775450,\\u0026quot;eop\\u0026quot;,469778129,\\u0026quot;eop\\u0026quot;,469778324,\\u0026quot;Default Paragraph Font\\u0026quot;]}\\"\\u003e\xe2\x80\x94 \\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/span\\u003epowered by Resource Watch, WRI\xe2\x80\x99s global open data platform \\u003cspan class=\\"TextRun SCXW236243878 BCX0\\" lang=\\"EN-GB\\" xml:lang=\\"EN-GB\\" data-contrast=\\"auto\\"\\u003e\\u003cspan class=\\"NormalTextRun SCXW236243878 BCX0\\" data-ccp-charstyle=\\"eop\\" data-ccp-charstyle-defn=\\"{\\u0026quot;ObjectId\\u0026quot;:\\u0026quot;6667d38c-8ac8-4f01-a3ed-b3f96323255f|69\\u0026quot;,\\u0026quot;ClassId\\u0026quot;:1073872969,\\u0026quot;Properties\\u0026quot;:[134233614,\\u0026quot;true\\u0026quot;,201340122,\\u0026quot;1\\u0026quot;,469775450,\\u0026quot;eop\\u0026quot;,469778129,\\u0026quot;eop\\u0026quot;,469778324,\\u0026quot;Default Paragraph Font\\u0026quot;]}\\"\\u003e\xe2\x80\x94\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/span\\u003e aims to help those managing ocean health find the answers they need to achieve global ocean goals.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-85091c1 elementor-widget elementor-widget-heading\\" data-id=\\"85091c1\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"heading.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\u003ch2 class=\\"elementor-heading-title elementor-size-default\\"\\u003e\\u003cb\\u003eCasting a Wide Net to Build a Robust Data Platform \\u003c/b\\u003e\\u003c/h2\\u003e\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-5a1c3fd7 elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"5a1c3fd7\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eThough there is an undeniable need for data on the ocean, simply putting data on a map is not enough. Effective data platforms must change mindsets and support equitable policy transformations, something which can only be achieved by exploring the challenges facing different ocean communities. It is also essential that any data platform in this space acknowledges these challenges are derived not only from a lack of data, but also larger socio-political considerations.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eQuestions are increasingly asked on how data is transformed into knowledge which then informs actions. Whose views are being privileged in the development of data platforms? Is the status quo being reinforced through the inclusion of certain datasets and the exclusion of others? Data scientists, no matter how intelligent or well-intentioned, cannot inform policy alone.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eTo construct the platform, 90 people \xe2\x80\x94 including academics, conservation organizations, NGOs representing local Indigenous groups and ocean policymakers \xe2\x80\x94 participated in an assessment designed to understand what problems exist in creating science-based ocean policies and how data could be provided in a way which would be most useful to them. Participants were from 20 different countries across five continents.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eMany similarities emerged in the responses across different groups. In particular, users repeatedly voiced five concerns which then helped inform and shape the design and development of Ocean Watch:\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003csection class=\\"elementor-section elementor-inner-section elementor-element elementor-element-b6010f7 elementor-section-boxed elementor-section-height-default elementor-section-height-default\\" data-id=\\"b6010f7\\" data-element_type=\\"section\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-container elementor-column-gap-default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-row\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-column elementor-col-50 elementor-inner-column elementor-element elementor-element-1f5bdaa\\" data-id=\\"1f5bdaa\\" data-element_type=\\"column\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-column-wrap elementor-element-populated\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-wrap\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-991b14d elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"991b14d\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003ch5\\u003e1. \xe2\x80\x9cI need to understand the impact of land management practices on ocean health\xe2\x80\x9d\\u003c/h5\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eIt is impossible to view the ocean in a holistic, integrated manner without considering what happens on land. It\xe2\x80\x99s the \xe2\x80\x9cupstream\xe2\x80\x9d of all the water which flows into the ocean. As a result, \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.science.org/doi/abs/10.1126/science.1109454\\"\\u003eforest management\\u003c/a\\u003e, \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.frontiersin.org/articles/10.3389/fmars.2019.00562/full\\"\\u003eagriculture\\u003c/a\\u003e and \\u003ca href=\\"https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s12237-019-00597-z\\"\\u003eurbanization\\u003c/a\\u003e each have a huge impact on ocean health.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eThis has become the defining feature of the first iteration of Ocean Watch. The platform acts as central space to understand what threats to the ocean are caused by impacts on the land. What impact is deforestation having? Where can reforestation help reduce nutrient pollution, which would otherwise damage coral reefs? Ocean Watch uses geospatial data to provide answers to these crucial questions, which can help inform land policies that also protect the ocean. For example, the map below provides clear information on which areas are at risk from erosion entering Nigerian water bodies.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-column elementor-col-50 elementor-inner-column elementor-element elementor-element-ec28908\\" data-id=\\"ec28908\\" data-element_type=\\"column\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-column-wrap elementor-element-populated\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-wrap\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-39edd29 elementor-widget elementor-widget-html\\" data-id=\\"39edd29\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"html.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv\\u003e\\u003ciframe src=\\"https://resourcewatch.org/embed/map/dc1135ea-3539-432a-acd5-d5ac0e6d127d?aoi=fa56e0796e2eac4eeecebc97a26b35ad\\" width=\\"100%\\" height=\\"500px\\" frameBorder=\\"0\\" /\\u003e\\u003c/iframe\\u003e \\u003c/div\\u003e\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-18dde97 elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"18dde97\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003e\\u003cem\\u003eFigure 1. Sources of erosion that are likely to enter water bodies, Nigeria\\u003c/em\\u003e\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\u003c/section\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-67a8ea76 elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"67a8ea76\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003ch5\\u003e2. \xe2\x80\x9cIndigenous and local communities need to be involved in decision-making\xe2\x80\x9d Co-leading\\u003c/h5\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eMany participants referenced the difficulties in achieving consensus across different groups when creating ocean policy, and particularly in ensuring the views of often marginalized people were listened to. Indigenous peoples and local communities currently oversee tens of thousands of kilometers of seabed along tropical coastlines and generally have a vastly different perspective on the challenges to preserving ocean biodiversity. A lack of shared understanding and difficulties in ensuring equitable access to data was suggested by many participants as a crucial barrier to co-leading effective management strategies on these lands. This can be particularly true when it comes to Indigenous people finding evidence to prove what they know is happening on their ancestral lands.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eTo an extent, these issues cannot (and arguably should not) be fixed by technology \xe2\x80\x94 a data platform alone cannot reorient society to return stewardship to Indigenous communities who were responsible for their environments for centuries. However, a data platform can seek to democratize access to ocean data by providing accessible tools built with reputable sources and satellite data. This data can inform policy discussions which involve many different parties, and its accessibility can enable a shared understanding among those parties.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003csection class=\\"elementor-section elementor-inner-section data-ccp-props=\\"{\\"\\u003e\xc2\xa0\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/h5\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eCurrently, ocean data is spread out across various systems, both public and private. There are global monitoring systems for mangroves, coral reefs, fishing and many other aspects of the ocean, but this siloed approach prevents users from seeing how they interact with each other.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eSustainable ocean management requires viewing the ocean as a whole ecosystem, not a disparate collection of services which have no impact on each other. The reality is that fishing impacts coral reefs; deforestation affects mangroves; mangroves and seagrasses reduce CO\\u003csub\\u003e2\\u003c/sub\\u003e\xc2\xa0emissions; and so on. data-ccp-props=\\"{\\"\\u003e\xc2\xa0\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/h5\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eMany participants in the user assessment indicated that platforms often have good data, but not tangible and accessible information. Many data platforms require users to have a geographic information system (GIS) background or a strong understanding of data science to effectively understand and interpret their information. However, sustainable ocean management requires data that is accessible and easy to interpret.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eFor example, users need an easy-to-use, curated primer on land-based pollution which allows them to access the information that participants identified as essential to effective policy. Every visualization on the Ocean Watch platform is downloadable, and all interactive maps and charts can be embedded in other webpages. Additionally, each element of the site comes with an option to see further information, giving fuller explanations of the data shown, the provenance of the information and possible implications.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-0dbbcc6 class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003ch5\\u003e5. \xe2\x80\x9cI need to see what I stand to lose\xe2\x80\x9d\xc2\xa0\\u003c/h5\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003ePrompting decision makers to take effective action requires giving people knowledge on what they stand to lose. Inevitably, all decisions require an element of trade off, and when asking people to prioritize ocean health over other economically important sectors like extensive fishing or mining, it becomes important to consider what other goods and services those ecosystems support.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eWho relies on the food generated by the ocean? How does the coastal zone support tourism? How much carbon could be stored in mangroves or seagrasses which reside in these ecosystems? Fundamentally, what will be destroyed if pressures such as land-based pollution and overfishing are left unchecked? These questions help to prompt decision-makers to stop and consider what is at stake if no action is taken, and this is the last point Ocean Watch seeks to drive home within the profiles for each location.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv elementor-size-default\\"\\u003eUsing Information to Protect the World\xe2\x80\x99s Oceans and Ecosystems \\u003c/h2\\u003e\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-7c384cd2 elementor-widget class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eWhile it is essential to bring together critical knowledge, the challenges facing the ocean cannot be addressed by technology alone. Even when data is available, deciphering where to start on such a wide-ranging and broad set of issues can feel as daunting as traversing the open ocean in a canoe.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eTransforming the ocean in an effective way will require different groups of people working together across wide-ranging and complex issues. True change will require practical implementation strategies, affordable financial support for those working on solutions and goal-setting that drives ambition. When paired with effective, participatory policymaking and more equitable practices, Ocean Watch aims to play an essential role to advance action, protect ocean health and preserve the ecosystems that so many depend on.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003e\\u003ca href=\\"https://resourcewatch.org/dashboards/ocean-watch\\"\\u003eOcean Watch\\u003c/a\\u003e is built on \\u003ca href=\\"https://resourcewatch.org/\\"\\u003eResource Watch\\u003c/a\\u003e, WRI\\u0026#8217;s data geospatial platform on planetary health. Resource Watch provides data visualization capabilities, an API and a global data catalogue, which has enabled a user-centered development of Ocean Watch and \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.wri.org/ocean\\"\\u003eWRI\\u0026#8217;s Ocean Program\\u003c/a\\u003e.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eThe first theme of Ocean Watch also aims to support the countries of the \\u003ca href=\\"http://www.oceanpanel.org/\\"\\u003eHigh Level Panel for a Sustainable Ocean Economy\\u003c/a\\u003e and their commitment to developing sustainable ocean plans to cover 100% of their national href=\\"https://blog.resourcewatch.org/author/caitlin-kontgis/\\" title=\\"Posts by Caitlin Kontgis\\" class=\\"author url fn\\" rel=\\"author\\"\\u003eCaitlin Kontgis\\u003c/a\\u003e, \\u003ca data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eRemote sensing has revolutionized how we measure and understand the Earth. We can now \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.globalforestwatch.org/map/?analysis=eyJzaG93QW5hbHlzaXMiOnRydWUsImhpZGRlbiI6ZmFsc2V9\\u0026amp;map=eyJ6b29tIjozLCJjZW50ZXIiOnsibGF0IjotNC4yMTQ5NDMxNDEzOTA2MzksImxuZyI6LTUuODAwNzgxMjUwMDAwMDAxfSwiY2FuQm91bmQiOmZhbHNlLCJiYm94IjpudWxsLCJkYXRhc2V0cyI6W3siZGF0YXNldCI6ImU2NjNlYjA5LTA0ZGUtNGYzOS1iODcxLTM1YzZjMmVkMTBiNSIsIm9wYWNpdHkiOjEsInZpc2liaWxpdHkiOnRydWUsImxheWVycyI6WyJkZDVkZjg3Zi0zOWMyLTRhZWItYTQ2Mi0zZWY5NjliMjBiNjYiXX0seyJkYXRhc2V0IjoiZmRjOGRjMWItMjcyOC00YTc5LWIyM2YtYjA5NDg1MDUyYjhkIiwibGF5ZXJzIjpbIjZmNjc5OGU2LTM5ZWMtNDE2My05NzllLTE4MmE3NGNhNjVlZSIsImM1ZDFlMDEwLTM4M2EtNDcxMy05YWFhLTQ0ZjcyOGMwNTcxYyJdLCJvcGFjaXR5IjoxLCJ2aXNpYmlsaXR5Ijp0cnVlfV19\\u0026amp;menu=eyJtZW51U2VjdGlvbiI6IiIsImRhdGFzZXRDYXRlZ29yeSI6IiJ9\\"\\u003etrack deforestation across the globe\\u003c/a\\u003e, \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.theverge.com/2016/8/4/12369494/descartes-artificial-intelligence-crop-predictions-usda\\"\\u003epredict end-of-season crop yields\\u003c/a\\u003e and \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.cnn.com/2019/12/05/tech/ai-wildfires/index.html\\"\\u003eidentify wildfires in near real-time\\u003c/a\\u003e. But exploration into its possibilities for urban areas has only just begun. \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.nrcan.gc.ca/maps-tools-and-publications/satellite-imagery-and-air-photos/remote-sensing-tutorials/land-cover-land-use/9373\\"\\u003eConventional land cover maps\\u003c/a\\u003e, which categorize the surface of the Earth into groupings like \\u0026#8220;forest\\u0026#8221; or \\u0026#8220;water\\u0026#8221; or \\u0026#8220;tundra,\\u0026#8221; often lump urban areas into a single category, like \\u0026#8220;urban\\u0026#8221; or \\u0026#8220;built-up.\\u0026#8221; This is useful for mapping urban extent generally, but does not capture the complexity of urban areas. Mapping land use, however, can reveal the patterns of a city, from road networks to housing availability to the distribution of commercial and industrial space \xe2\x80\x94 along with the jobs they represent \xe2\x80\x94 and much more.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eMapping urban land use over time can show what, where and when changes are happening: where the city is expanding or contracting; what patterns and densities characterize areas of growth or redevelopment; and which types of land use are being displaced. This information, for example, can highlight spatial inequality and other key issues for cities. Has housing kept pace with the population? Has infrastructure kept pace with development, and if not, where is it needed? Is growth encroaching on wetlands or farmlands that are critical to the city\\u0026#8217;s well-being? Pressing questions like these abound for urban planners, officials and residents. Robust land use data can help provide the answers.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cdiv\\u003e\\u003ciframe src=\\"https://resourcewatch.org/embed/data/explore?section=Discover\\u0026amp;zoom=12.531206674880647\\u0026amp;lat=25.726863440879296\\u0026amp;lng=-100.18635080816763\\u0026amp;pitch=0\\u0026amp;bearing=0\\u0026amp;basemap=satellite\\u0026amp;labels=light\\u0026amp;layers=%255B%257B%2522dataset%2522%253A%2522e1c519d3-16ea-400a-a71c-9033ba5f490b%2522%252C%2522opacity%2522%253A0.7%252C%2522layer%2522%253A%252224e3f5c5-396b-48c5-b89a-5a680278b612%2522%257D%252C%257B%2522dataset%2522%253A%2522dfbf97c3-ee82-4c68-808b-3bcc60e57167%2522%252C%2522opacity%2522%253A0.7%252C%2522layer%2522%253A%252224c07a2d-f065-431e-a29e-de1351ed4310%2522%257D%255D\\u0026amp;page=1\\u0026amp;sort=most-viewed\\u0026amp;sortDirection=-1\\" width=\\"100%\\" height=\\"500px\\" frameborder=\\"0\\"\\u003e\\u003c/iframe\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-7310f9a elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"7310f9a\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003e\\u003cem\\u003eClose-up view of WRI\xe2\x80\x99s six-category urban land use and road maps for northeast Monterrey urban area, Mexico.\\u003c/em\\u003e\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-4edbb0c elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"4edbb0c\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eWRI, with support from the National Geographic Society, has developed methods and infrastructure to\xc2\xa0\\u003ca href=\\"https://www.wri.org/publication/mapping-urban-land-use-in-india-and-mexico\\"\\u003emap urban land use in any city\\u003c/a\\u003e, providing a new tool to help cities manage their resources and improve quality of life. The results for cities in two countries, Mexico and India, illustrate what makes these new urban land use maps novel and how they can benefit cities.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-490212dd elementor-widget elementor-widget-heading\\" data-id=\\"490212dd\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"heading.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\u003ch1 class=\\"elementor-heading-title elementor-size-default\\"\\u003eMapping Patterns of Life\\u003c/h1\\u003e\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-409730c elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"409730c\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eMore than half of the world\\u0026#8217;s population now lives in cities, but there\\u0026#8217;s still a lot we don\\u0026#8217;t know about urban areas. This is especially true for rapidly growing cities in emerging economies, where expansion and redevelopment often outpace administrative capacity. From the city scale to the neighborhood scale, there is little rigorous, globally-consistent data on how cities are arranged, how they grow and change and how to improve them for the well-being of urban residents and the planet.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eDetailed, global maps of land use within cities have, to date, simply not existed. \\u003ca href=\\"https://land.copernicus.eu/pan-european/corine-land-cover\\"\\u003eMany\\u003c/a\\u003e \\u003ca href=\\"https://modis.gsfc.nasa.gov/data/dataprod/mod12.php\\"\\u003eexisting\\u003c/a\\u003e \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.esa-landcover-cci.org/\\"\\u003eproducts\\u003c/a\\u003e show land cover at the continental or global scale and are spatially coarse. Other, true land use remote products are based on expensive, relatively scarce high-resolution satellite imagery, and are thus limited to individual cities or even districts. Other land use maps are created by city planners through detailed, on-the-ground data collection to develop \\u003ca href=\\"http://www.fao.org/3/v4860e/v4860e03.htm\\"\\u003ecadasters\\u003c/a\\u003e.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eTo address this information gap, we used data from the \\u003ca href=\\"http://www.atlasofurbanexpansion.org/\\"\\u003eAtlas of Urban Expansion\\u003c/a\\u003e, remote sensing imagery, machine learning techniques and cloud computing tools \xe2\x80\x94 including Python libraries, Keras and the \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.descarteslabs.com/\\"\\u003eDescartes Labs Platform\\u003c/a\\u003e \xe2\x80\x94 to create computer vision models to categorize and map land use.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eOur new urban mapping system is different: the resulting maps feature a detailed taxonomy of land use drawn at 5-meter resolution and require only medium-resolution satellite imagery, which is publicly available for the Earth\xe2\x80\x99s entire surface and is constantly updated.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eThanks to the imagery archives of ESA\xe2\x80\x99s Sentinel and NASA\xe2\x80\x99s Landsat satellite constellations, we can retroactively map urban land use going back years. And because each data set captures the full globe at least a couple of times per month, our methodology can continually be applied to new imagery, creating an up-to-date and ever-richer dataset that can provide insights about how cities around the world are growing and changing. The outputs are \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.wri.org/publication/mapping-urban-land-use-in-india-and-mexico\\"\\u003epublicly available\\u003c/a\\u003e so urban planners and other practitioners can start using them in research and to inform decisions immediately.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-2e1aaf1 elementor-widget elementor-widget-heading\\" data-id=\\"2e1aaf1\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"heading.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\u003ch1 class=\\"elementor-heading-title elementor-size-default\\"\\u003eInsights from Hyderabad and Mexico City\\u003c/h1\\u003e\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-dd0383a elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"dd0383a\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eUsing these models, we mapped land use across multiple cities in Mexico and India, two rapidly urbanizing countries with major differences in their urban land use and development history. Despite having some of the largest cities globally, India is still mostly rural, with only\xc2\xa0\\u003ca href=\\"https://databank.worldbank.org/reports.aspx?source=2\\u0026amp;series=SP.URB.TOTL.IN.ZS\\u0026amp;country=IND\\"\\u003e34%\\u003c/a\\u003e\xc2\xa0of its population living in urban areas. In contrast,\xc2\xa0\\u003ca href=\\"https://databank.worldbank.org/reports.aspx?source=2\\u0026amp;series=SP.URB.TOTL.IN.ZS\\u0026amp;country=MEX\\"\\u003e80%\\u003c/a\\u003e\xc2\xa0of Mexico\xe2\x80\x99s population is considered urban.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eSide-by-side comparisons of WRI\xe2\x80\x99s land use maps (5 m spatial resolution) and the ESA CCI land cover maps (300 m resolution) illustrate the improved level of detail achieved in this new dataset. In the ESA land cover maps, both Hyderabad, India\xc2\xa0and Mexico City, Mexico\xc2\xa0look like giant blobs of \xe2\x80\x9curban\xe2\x80\x9d across the landscape: they lack definition at the boundaries and offer little detail about the city\xe2\x80\x99s interior landscape. Within the urban class, there is no information about areas with primarily residential versus primarily business activities, the location of transportation corridors or where infrastructure exists. All of these elements are critical to understanding the specific, local urbanization challenges faced by a city.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-44630ba elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"44630ba\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cdiv\\u003e\\u003ciframe src=\\"https://resourcewatch.org/embed/map-swipe?zoom=8.945289757559998\\u0026amp;lat=19.400853623283876\\u0026amp;lng=-99.09470695702\\u0026amp;layers=68a50d22-a821-4a39-bb1b-d51fd5fa85c9,24c07a2d-f065-431e-a29e-de1351ed4310\\" width=\\"100%\\" height=\\"500px\\" frameborder=\\"0\\"\\u003e\\u003c/iframe\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-ff7543a elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"ff7543a\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003e\\u003cem\\u003eESA CCI land cover map (left, 300 meter spatial resolution) compared to WRI\xe2\x80\x99s urban land use map (right, 5 meter spatial resolution) for Mexico City, Mexico.\\u003c/em\\u003e\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-0d6adc9 elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"0d6adc9\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eThe finer-resolution maps developed through this model distinguish details in these \xe2\x80\x9cblobs,\xe2\x80\x9d revealing patterns and details invisible at coarser scales. For example, the largest non-residential regions in Mexico City are in the northern portion of the metropolitan area, where industrial uses and warehouses are common. Housing types that serve low-income people (informal, atomistic and residential projects) are also common near these non-residential districts in the north, as well as along the city\xe2\x80\x99s periphery. Formal housing is predominant in the city center and south. The \\u003ca href=\\"https://thecityfix.com/blog/watch-urban-growth-unfold-amazing-visualizations-cities-worldwide-accra-mexico-city-nairobi-istanbul-sustaianble-development-sprawl-coby-joseph/\\"\\u003e(in)famous sprawl of the Mexico City metropolitan area\\u003c/a\\u003e and the relative spatial segregation of land uses contributes to long commutes, especially for those living at the periphery, and is a significant contributor to the capital\xe2\x80\x99s \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/2019/05/16/scary-images-mexico-citys-pollution-emergency/\\"\\u003ewell-documented air pollution\\u003c/a\\u003e.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eBy contrast, concentrations of non-residential areas in Hyderabad are largely found on the periphery, many of which represent the information technology office parks that proliferated at the city\xe2\x80\x99s edge over the past few decades. This also meant significant \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.worldbank.org/en/news/feature/2013/10/21/india-urbanization-report-beyond-sustainable-cities\\"\\u003eemployment and housing growth in suburban areas\\u003c/a\\u003e, which has \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.wri.org/events/2019/01/upward-and-outward-growth\\"\\u003estressed the city\xe2\x80\x99s ability to provide services\\u003c/a\\u003e.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eThe pattern of informal settlements also distinctly differs between the two cities. In Mexico City, whose metropolitan population increased an average of \\u003ca href=\\"http://atlasofurbanexpansion.org/cities/view/Mexico_City\\"\\u003e2.5% per year\\u003c/a\\u003e since 1990, rapid growth spawned both informal residential areas and \xe2\x80\x9catomistic settlements\xe2\x80\x9d \xe2\x80\x94 areas that were not clearly subdivided and grew incrementally. These areas represent both planned developments to accommodate new residents (as evidenced in Chimalhuacan and surrounding municipalities, the large area of \xe2\x80\x9cinformal subdivisions\xe2\x80\x9d in the southeast) and unplanned growth when housing efforts did not keep pace or meet residential needs (often atomistic settlements found primarily along the urban periphery and into the foothills of the mountains that surround the Valle de M\xc3\xa9xico). Many of these areas lack the basic infrastructure that other settlement areas enjoy, such as reliable water, sanitation, electricity and public transportation. People living in these areas also have more \\u003ca href=\\"https://thecityfix.com/blog/map-month-mobility-health-education-inequality-mexico-city-spatial-problem-mauricio-brito-lorelei-ramirez-reyes-jorge-macias-eric-mackres/\\"\\u003edifficulty accessing critical urban services\\u003c/a\\u003e like jobs, education, food, recreation and health care. Traditional land cover maps do not reflect these distinctions in land use type, or the associated characteristics and problems.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eHyderabad is different: its unplanned settlements, many of which are long established, are distributed throughout the core of the city, along the periphery and in surrounding villages. The informal residential areas and non-residential areas that dot the region surrounding the city are typical of many South and Southeast Asian cities. These \xe2\x80\x9c\\u003ca href=\\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desakota\\"\\u003edesakota\\u003c/a\\u003e\xe2\x80\x9d regions have urban characteristics but are also highly reliant on agriculture. Many of these areas are already subsumed by the growing city, transformed into \xe2\x80\x9curban villages,\xe2\x80\x9d with more areas likely to follow as the city grows, creating an even more sprawling megacity. As these unconnected dots grow into the more consolidated and contiguous city, monitoring land use change offers the opportunity to anticipate and manage these challenges.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-d46e40b class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cdiv\\u003e\\u003ciframe src=\\"https://resourcewatch.org/embed/map-swipe?zoom=9.93178667264047\\u0026amp;lat=17.38006432582498\\u0026amp;lng=78.51099432114907\\u0026amp;layers=68a50d22-a821-4a39-bb1b-d51fd5fa85c9,f62e9230-6e64-43a8-b7ae-f6f4e3188758\\" width=\\"100%\\" height=\\"500px\\" frameborder=\\"0\\"\\u003e\\u003c/iframe\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-c56c2a6 elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"c56c2a6\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003e\\u003cem\\u003eESA CCI land cover map (left, 300 meter spatial resolution) compared to WRI\xe2\x80\x99s urban land use map (right, 5 meter spatial resolution) for Hyderabad, India.\\u003c/em\\u003e\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-48e53f2 elementor-widget elementor-widget-heading\\" data-id=\\"48e53f2\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"heading.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\u003ch1 class=\\"elementor-heading-title elementor-size-default\\"\\u003e\\u003ch1 data-elementor-setting-key=\\"title\\" data-pen-placeholder=\\"Type Here...\\" style=\\"font-weight: 300;line-height: 1em;font-size: 64px;letter-spacing: -1.5px\\"\\u003eImplications\\u003c/h1\\u003e\\u003c/h1\\u003e\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-3f89afd elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"3f89afd\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eThere are numerous ways that fine-grained land use maps like these can be utilized, as researchers can compare patterns within cities and differences from city to city and country to country. These land use data can combine with other datasets \xe2\x80\x94 such as data on the socioeconomics of households, amenities and services, land values, economic activity, hazards and vulnerabilities \xe2\x80\x94 to derive new insights.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eBased on these findings, policymakers, civil society and the private sector can make changes on the ground to improve peoples\xe2\x80\x99 lives, including enabling better targeting of scarce resources based on evidence. And over time, these data can be used to measure the effectiveness of the \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.un.org/sustainabledevelopment/sustainable-development-goals/\\"\\u003eU.N. Sustainable Development Goals\\u003c/a\\u003e and other development metrics.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003eWe continue to develop and improve our methodology and aim, pending necessary resources, to ultimately produce equivalent maps for every city in the world every year. With high-fidelity land use data like these, researchers can better understand how urban areas develop over time, how land use changes along the urban periphery and which types of settlements are most affected by natural disasters such as flooding or landslides. These are just a few possible applications, but the potential for these data are even greater \xe2\x80\x94 and can only be fully realized by putting these maps and methods in the hands of users.\\u003c/p\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-element elementor-element-0c7a9c6 elementor-widget elementor-widget-text-editor\\" data-id=\\"0c7a9c6\\" data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003cp\\u003e\\u003cem\\u003eAccess the \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.wri.org/publication/mapping-urban-land-use-in-india-and-mexico\\"\\u003etechnical note\\u003c/a\\u003e, \\u003ca href=\\"https://github.com/wri/UrbanLandUse/releases/tag/v0.2.0\\"\\u003eopen source scripts\\u003c/a\\u003e and resulting maps (\\u003ca href=\\"https://resourcewatch.org/data/explore/cit049-Urban-Land-Use-India_1\\"\\u003eIndia\\u003c/a\\u003e, \\u003ca href=\\"https://resourcewatch.org/data/explore/cit047-Urban-Land-Use-Mexico\\"\\u003eMexico\\u003c/a\\u003e, \\u003ca href=\\"https://resourcewatch.org/data/explore/cit048-Urban-Land-Use-Mexico-Roads\\"\\u003eMexico roads\\u003c/a\\u003e). data-element_type=\\"widget\\" data-widget_type=\\"text-editor.default\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-widget-container\\"\\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\u003cdiv class=\\"elementor-text-editor elementor-clearfix\\"\\u003e\\u003ch1\\u003e\\u003ca href=\\"https://www.crowtherlab.com/\\"\\u003e\\u003cimg class=\\"aligncenter wp-image-5195 size-large\\" src=\\"http://blog.resourcewatch.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Logo-ETH-CL_black-and-yellow_outlined-1-1024x175.png\\" alt=\\"\\" width=\\"800\\" height=\\"137\\" /\\u003e\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003c/h1\\u003e\\n\\u003ch1\\u003e\\u003ci style=\\"color: inherit; font-family: inherit; font-size: 2.5rem;\\"\\u003eCrowther Lab \\u0026#8211; A Resource Watch Partner Profile\\u003c/i\\u003e\\u003c/h1\\u003e\\n\\u003cdiv\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003eClimate change and biodiversity loss are among the two greatest threats facing society \xe2\x80\x93 and they are intrinsically linked. Preserving terrestrial ecosystems is of the utmost importance if we want to protect our environment and our communities. Understanding those ecosystems is a key step to informing how to protect and restore them.\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\u003ciframe src=\\"https://resourcewatch.org/embed/map/2826f473-9200-4bdc-9ab1-75bea34bbb21\\" width=\\"100%\\" height=\\"500px\\" frameBorder=\\"0\\" scrolling=\\"yes\\"\\u003e\\u003c/iframe\\u003e\\n\\u003cspan\\u003e\\u003cdiv\\u003eAt the \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.crowtherlab.com/\\"\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003eCrowther Lab\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003e (\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003ca href=\\"https://ethz.ch/en.html\\"\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003eETH Zurich\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003e), we create scientific models \\u0026#8211; often in the form of spatially explicit global maps \\u0026#8211; which help give us a new or better understanding of Earth\xe2\x80\x99s ecosystems. These maps not only inform us about current\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003ca href=\\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?time_continue=73\\u0026amp;v=w9UkMmtbn7E\\u0026amp;feature=emb_logo\\"\\u003e \\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003eecological diversity\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003e, but we are now also starting to generate an understanding of ecological potential, e.g. how much vegetative carbon could be supported on the planet, at both global and regional scales. Our lab was founded on the belief that it is only with a global perspective of all ecological ecosystems, be they above or below ground, can society define effective targets and strategies for nature-based solutions.\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\u003cdiv\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\u003cdiv\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003eBut, every good model and map starts with data. Lots of data. We work with global networks of scientific collaborators (including the\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003ca href=\\"https://www.gfbinitiative.org/\\"\\u003e \\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003eGlobal Forest Biodiversity Initiative\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003e and the\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003ca href=\\"https://www.globalsoilbiodiversity.org/\\"\\u003e \\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003eGlobal Soil Biodiversity Initiative\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003e) to build and analyze large databases of ground truthed observations. These databases currently consist of more than 30 million measurements of biodiversity, where scientists have painstakingly identified tree species and \\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003ca href=\\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=lfU5BIbln9Y\\"\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003emeasured \\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003ethem \\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003ewith diameter tapes and height sticks, or collected soil samples using \\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003ca href=\\"https://www.ams-samplers.com/hand-tooling/soil-samplers/soil-core-samplers.html\\"\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003esoil cores\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003e, collection bags and so on. We also look at databases with information about the physical environment such as precipitation and temperature, and sometimes even satellite imagery. After identifying relationships and patterns between the ecological and environmental variables, we then use machine learning models to extend those patterns across the globe to generate spatially explicit information (e.g. data maps about trees and soil) with a \\u003ca href=\\"https://www.nature.com/articles/s41586-019-1418-6\\"\\u003ehigher level of predictive accuracy\\u003c/a\\u003e.\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\u003ch4\\u003e\\u003cb data-test=\\"figure-caption-text\\"\\u003eGlobal map of soil nematode density at the 30\xc2\xa0arcsec (approximately 1\xc2\xa0km\\u003csup\\u003e2\\u003c/sup\\u003e) pixel scale, created by the Crowther Lab.\\u003c/b\\u003e\\u003c/h4\\u003e\\n\\u003cfigure id=\\"attachment_5093\\" aria-describedby=\\"caption-attachment-5093\\" style=\\"width: 9351px\\" class=\\"wp-caption aligncenter\\"\\u003e\\u003ca href=\\"https://www.nature.com/articles/s41586-019-1418-6\\"\\u003e\\u003cimg src=\\"http://blog.resourcewatch.org/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Fig3_final_updated.png\\" alt=\\"Global map of soil nematode density at the 30 arcsec (approximately 1 km2) pixel scale.\\" width=\\"9351\\" height=\\"3695\\" /\\u003e\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003cfigcaption id=\\"caption-attachment-5093\\" class=\\"wp-caption-text\\"\\u003evan den Hoogen et al., 2019\\u003c/figcaption\\u003e\\u003c/figure\\u003e\\n\\n\\u003cdiv\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\u003cdiv\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003eWe hope these maps will provide the scientific basis to guide restoration and conservation organizations, providing insights as to which parts of the world we could focus on if we are going to address one of the greatest threats to modern society.\xc2\xa0\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\u003cdiv\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\u003cdiv\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003eThe process of creating data, providing insight, and effecting change can be a complex and lengthy one. An example is an ongoing collaboration with\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003ca href=\\"https://resourcewatch.org/\\"\\u003e \\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003eResource Watch\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003e to support\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003ca href=\\"https://gouritz.com/\\"\\u003e \\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003eGouritz Cluster Biosphere Reserve\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003e (GCBR), a nonprofit dedicated to protecting the reserve\xe2\x80\x99s nature and biodiversity and a partner of ours through founding partner,\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003ca href=\\"https://www.dobecology.nl/\\"\\u003e \\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003eDOB Ecology\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003e. This collaboration, while still in very early stages, is an exciting case study for how our models can be trained, using ground truthed data, to function at a much finer scale. Through this collaboration with GCBR and Resource Watch, we can take global satellite data to the ground in a way that wasn\\u0026#8217;t possible before.\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\u003cdiv\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\u003cdiv\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003eIf we are able to apply scientific models with this level of predictive accuracy, at such a fine scale, and high resolution, it could transform how we plan, monitor and improve restoration projects around the world.\xc2\xa0\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\u003cdiv\\u003e\\u003c/div\\u003e\\n\\u003cdiv\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003eIf you are interested in learning more about Crowther Lab\xe2\x80\x99s work and how we are uniting global models and satellite data with ground truthing, please visit our \\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003ca href=\\"https://www.crowtherlab.com/restoration/\\"\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003ewebsite\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003e and join the network of restoration practitioners we are working with \\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003ca href=\\"https://www.crowtherlab.com/restoration/#sign-up\\"\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight: 400;\\"\\u003ehere\\u003c/span\\u003e\\u003c/a\\u003e\\u003cspan style=\\"font-weight:
